In Mollet's view, his fidelity to NATO had earned him the right to expect firm American support against Egypt, and when that support proved not forthcoming, he became even more determined that if the Americans were not willing to do anything about Nasser, then France would act.[[125]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Kyle,_Keith,_p._156-130)[_[additional citation(s) needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

### Commonwealth response

Among the "White Dominions" of the [British Commonwealth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations "Commonwealth of Nations"), Canada had few ties with the Suez Canal and twice had refused British requests for peacetime military aid in the Middle East. It had little reaction to the seizure before military action. By 1956 the [Panama Canal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panama_Canal "Panama Canal") was much more important than Suez to Australia and New Zealand; the following year two experts would write that it "is not vital to the [Australian economy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Australia "Economy of Australia")". The memory, however, of the two nations fighting in two world wars to protect a canal which many still called their "lifeline" to Britain or "jugular vein", contributed to Australian Prime Minister [Robert Menzies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Menzies "Robert Menzies") and New Zealand Prime Minister [Sidney Holland](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sidney_Holland "Sidney Holland") supporting Britain in the early weeks following the seizure. On 7 August Holland hinted to his parliament that New Zealand might send troops to assist Britain, and received support from the opposition. On 13 August, Menzies, who had travelled to London from the United States after hearing of the nationalisation and became an informal member of the [British Cabinet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom "Cabinet of the United Kingdom") discussing the issue, spoke on the BBC in support of the Eden government's position on the canal. He called the dispute over the canal "a crisis more grave than any since the Second World War ended".[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 13–16, 56–58, 84  An elder statesman of the Commonwealth who felt that Nasser's actions threatened trading nations like Australia, he argued publicly that Western powers had built the canal but that Egypt was now seeking to exclude them from a role in its ownership or management.[[126]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-ReferenceB-131)[[127]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-ReferenceC-132) South Africa's [Johannes Strijdom](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Strijdom "Johannes Strijdom") stated "it is best to keep our heads out of the beehive". His government saw Nasser as an enemy but would benefit economically and geopolitically from a closed canal, and diplomatically from [not opposing a nation's right to govern its internal affairs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_South_Africa_during_apartheid "Foreign relations of South Africa during apartheid").[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 16–18

The "non-white Dominions" saw Egypt's seizing of the canal as an admirable act of [anti-imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-imperialism "Anti-imperialism"), and Nasser's Arab nationalism as similar to Asian nationalism. Indian Prime Minister [Jawaharlal Nehru](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru "Jawaharlal Nehru") was with Nasser when he learned of the Anglo-American withdrawal of aid for the Aswan Dam. As India was a major user of the canal, however, he remained publicly neutral other than warning that any use of force, or threats, could be "disastrous". Suez was also very important to the [Dominion of Ceylon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon "Dominion of Ceylon")'s economy, and it was renegotiating defence treaties with Britain, so its government was not as vocal in supporting Egypt as it would have likely been otherwise. Pakistan was also cautious about supporting Egypt given their rivalry as leading Islamic nations, but its government did state that Nasser had the right to nationalise.[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 18–24, 79

### Western diplomacy

On 1 August 1956, a tripartite meeting was opened at [10 Downing Street](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/10_Downing_Street "10 Downing Street") between British Foreign Secretary [Selwyn Lloyd](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selwyn_Lloyd "Selwyn Lloyd"), U.S. Ambassador [Robert D. Murphy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Daniel_Murphy "Robert Daniel Murphy") and French Foreign Affairs Minister [Christian Pineau](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Pineau "Christian Pineau").[[128]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-133)

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Portrait_Menzies_1950s.jpg)

Australian Prime Minister [Robert Menzies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Menzies "Robert Menzies") led an international committee in negotiations with Nasser in September 1956, which sought to achieve international management of the Suez Canal. The mission was a failure.

Almost immediately after the nationalisation, Eisenhower suggested to Eden a conference of maritime nations that used the canal. The British preferred to invite the most important countries, but the Americans believed that inviting as many as possible amid maximum publicity would affect world opinion. Invitations went to the eight surviving signatories of the [Constantinople Convention](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convention_of_Constantinople "Convention of Constantinople") and the 16 other largest users of the canal: Australia, Ceylon, Denmark, Egypt, Ethiopia, France, West Germany, Greece, India, Indonesia, Iran, Italy, Japan, the Netherlands, New Zealand, Norway, Pakistan, Portugal, Soviet Union, Spain, Sweden, Turkey, the United Kingdom, and the United States. All except Egypt—which sent an observer, and used India and the Soviet Union to represent its interests—and Greece accepted the invitation, and the 22 nations' representatives met in London from 16 to 23 August.[[129]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-life19560827-134)[[130]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKingseed199566%E2%80%9367-135)[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 81–89

Fifteen of the nations supported the American-British-French position of international operation of the canal; Pakistan chose its western allies over its sympathy for Egypt's anti-western position despite resulting great domestic controversy. Ceylon, Indonesia, and the Soviet Union supported India's competing proposal—which Nasser had preapproved—of international supervision only. India criticised Egypt's seizure of the canal, but insisted that its ownership and operation now not change. The majority of 18 chose five nations to negotiate with Nasser in Cairo led by Menzies, while their proposal for international operation of the canal would go to the Security Council.[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 81–89 [[126]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-ReferenceB-131)[[130]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKingseed199566%E2%80%9367-135)

Menzies' 7 September official communique to Nasser presented a case for compensation for the Suez Canal Company and the "establishment of principles" for the future use of the canal that would ensure that it would "continue to be an international waterway operated free of politics or national discrimination, and with financial structure so secure and an international confidence so high that an expanding and improving future for the Canal could be guaranteed" and called for a convention to recognise Egyptian sovereignty of the canal, but for the establishment of an international body to run the canal. Nasser saw such measures as a "derogation from Egyptian sovereignty" and rejected Menzies' proposals.[[126]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-ReferenceB-131) Menzies hinted to Nasser that Britain and France might use force to resolve the crisis, but Eisenhower openly opposed the use of force and Menzies left Egypt without success.[[127]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-ReferenceC-132)

Instead of the 18-nation proposal, the United States proposed an association of canal users that would set rules for its operation. Whereas 14 of the other nations, not including Pakistan, agreed. Britain, in particular, believed that violation of the association rules would result in military force, but after Eden made a speech to this effect in parliament on 12 September, the US Ambassador Dulles insisted "...we do not intend to shoot our way through" the canal.[[115]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-eayrs1964-120): 89–92  The United States worked through diplomatic channels to resolve the crisis without military conflict. "The British and French reluctantly agreed to pursue the diplomatic avenue but viewed it as merely an attempt to buy time, during which they continued their military preparations."[[131]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-136) The British, [Washington's closest ally](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Relationship "Special Relationship"), disregarded Eisenhower's argument that the American people would not accept a military solution.[[132]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-137)

On 25 September 1956 the Chancellor of the Exchequer [Harold Macmillan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harold_Macmillan "Harold Macmillan") met informally with Eisenhower at the [White House](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House"). Macmillan doubted that Eisenhower had a determination to avoid war, and told Eden that the Americans would not in any way oppose the attempt to topple Nasser.[[133]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-138) The Americans refused to support any move that could be seen as [imperialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism") or [colonialism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism"), seeing the US as the champion of [decolonisation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonization "Decolonization"). Eisenhower felt the crisis had to be handled peacefully; he told Eden that American public opinion, and the international community, "would be outraged" unless all peaceful routes had been exhausted, and even then "the eventual price might become far too heavy".[[134]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-139)[[135]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-140) Eden and other leading British officials believed Nasser's support for [Palestinian fedayeen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_fedayeen "Palestinian fedayeen") against Israel, as well as his attempts to destabilise pro-western regimes in Iraq and other Arab states, would deter the US from intervening with the operation. London believed that Nasser's engagement with communist states would persuade the Americans to accept British and French actions if they were presented as a _[fait accompli](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fait\_accompli "Fait accompli")_.[_[citation needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

Motives for invading Egypt
--------------------------

See also: [Protocol of Sèvres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_of_S%C3%A8vres "Protocol of Sèvres")

### Britain and France

Britain was anxious lest it lose efficient access to the remains of its empire. Both Britain and France were eager that the canal should remain open as an important conduit of oil.[_[citation needed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

Both the French and the British felt that Nasser should be removed from power. The French "held the Egyptian president responsible for assisting the anti-colonial rebellion in Algeria".[[136]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-141) France was nervous about the growing influence that Nasser exerted on its North African colonies and protectorates.

### Israel

On the eve of the invasion, [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") outlined to [Guy Mollet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guy_Mollet "Guy Mollet"), the French Prime minister, his plan for a 'new order' in the Middle East. This consisted of (a) Israel occupying and annexing both the Gaza Strip and the Sinai; (b) an Israeli annexation of [Southern Lebanon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Lebanon "Southern Lebanon"), and the creation of a [Christian Maronite state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maronites "Maronites") in the remaining territory; (c) the dismantling of Jordan by dividing its land between Israel and Iraq, with Israel annexing the [West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank") and Iraq undertaking in a peace treaty to absorb the Palestinian refugees in the former, and in Jordanian refugee camps. Aspiring also to overthrow Nasser, the plan foresaw Israeli exercising control over the [Gulf of Aqaba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Aqaba "Gulf of Aqaba").[[137]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-142)

Israel wanted to reopen the [Straits of Tiran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Straits_of_Tiran "Straits of Tiran") leading to the Gulf of Aqaba to Israeli shipping, and saw the opportunity to strengthen its southern border and to weaken what it saw as a dangerous and hostile state. This was particularly felt in the form of attacks injuring approximately 1,300 civilians emanating from the Egyptian-held [Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip"),[[138]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-143) during the period of [Israel's Border Wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%27s_Border_Wars,_1949%E2%80%931956 "Israel's Border Wars, 1949–1956").

The Israelis were also deeply troubled by Egypt's procurement of large amounts of Soviet weaponry that included 530 armoured vehicles, of which 230 were tanks; 500 guns; 150 [MiG-15](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MiG-15 "MiG-15") jet fighters; 50 [Ilyushin Il-28](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-28 "Ilyushin Il-28") bombers; submarines and other naval craft. The influx of this advanced weaponry altered an already shaky balance of power.[[139]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchiff197465%E2%80%9366-144) Israel was alarmed by the Czechoslovak arms deal,[_[which?](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid\_weasel\_words "Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words")_] and believed it had only a narrow window of opportunity to hit Egypt's army.[[140]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Kandil2012p47-145) Additionally, Israel believed Egypt had formed a secret alliance with Jordan and Syria.[[141]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-146)

Notably, the strategic alignment of Israel and Britain leading up to the Suez invasion, as represented in the [Protocol of Sèvres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_of_S%C3%A8vres "Protocol of Sèvres"), "marked the end of the estrangement between [Britain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") and the [Zionist movement](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_movement "Zionist movement") that went back to the [White Paper of 1939](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Paper_of_1939 "White Paper of 1939")."[[142]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-147)

Forces
------

### British

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1956-08-06_Suez_Crisis.ogv "Play video")Duration: 6 minutes and 23 seconds.6:23 Subtitles available.CC[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1956-08-06_Suez_Crisis.ogv)

Universal Newsreel from 6 August about the departure of British and French ships for Egypt

British troops were well-trained, experienced, and had good morale, but suffered from the economic and technological limitations imposed by post-war austerity.[[143]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._15-148) The 16th Independent Parachute Brigade Group, which was intended to be the main British strike force against Egypt, was heavily involved in the [Cyprus Emergency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus_Emergency "Cyprus Emergency"), which led to a neglect of paratroop training in favour of [counter-insurgency operations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterinsurgency "Counterinsurgency").[[143]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._15-148) The [Royal Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") could project formidable power through the guns of its warships and aircraft flown from its carriers, but lacked amphibious capability.[[144]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._16-149)

The [Royal Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Navy "Royal Navy") had just undergone a major and innovative carrier modernisation program. The [Royal Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Air_Force "Royal Air Force") (RAF) had just introduced two [long-range bombers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long-range_bomber "Long-range bomber"), the [Vickers Valiant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vickers_Valiant "Vickers Valiant") and the [English Electric Canberra](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Electric_Canberra "English Electric Canberra"), but owing to their recent entry into service the RAF had not yet established proper bombing techniques for these aircraft.[[144]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._16-149) Despite this, General [Charles Keightley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Keightley "Charles Keightley"), the commander of the invasion force, believed that [air power](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airpower "Airpower") alone was sufficient to defeat Egypt.[[144]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._16-149) By contrast, General [Hugh Stockwell](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugh_Stockwell "Hugh Stockwell"), the Task Force's ground commander, believed that methodical and systematic armoured operations centred on the [Centurion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centurion_tank "Centurion tank") battle tank would be the key to victory.[[145]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-150)

### French

French troops were experienced and well-trained but suffered from cutbacks imposed by post-war politics of economic austerity.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) In 1956, the [French Armed Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Armed_Forces "French Armed Forces") was heavily involved in the Algerian war, which made operations against Egypt a major distraction.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) French paratroopers of the elite _[Regiment de Parachutistes Coloniaux](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2nd\_Marine\_Infantry\_Parachute\_Regiment "2nd Marine Infantry Parachute Regiment")_ (RPC) were extremely experienced, battle-hardened, and very tough soldiers, who had greatly distinguished themselves in the fighting in Indochina and in Algeria.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) The men of the RPC followed a "shoot first, ask questions later" policy towards civilians, first adopted in Vietnam, which was to lead to the killing of a number of Egyptian civilians.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) The rest of the French troops were described by the American military historian Derek Varble as "competent, but not outstanding".[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151)

The main French (and Israeli) tank, the [AMX-13](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AMX-13 "AMX-13"), was designed for mobile, flanking operations, which led to a tank that was lightly armoured but agile.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) General [André Beaufre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Beaufre "André Beaufre"), who served as Stockwell's subordinate, favoured a swift campaign of movement in which the main objective was to encircle the enemy.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) Throughout the operation, Beaufre proved himself to be more aggressive than his British counterparts, always urging that some bold step be taken at once.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151) The [French Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Navy "French Navy") had a powerful carrier force which was excellent for projecting power inland, but, like its British counterpart, suffered from a lack of landing craft.[[146]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._17-151)

### Israeli

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:AMX-13_at_Latrun4.JPG)

An Israeli [AMX-13](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/AMX-13 "AMX-13"), shown here from the rear and side

American military historian Derek Varble called the [Israel Defense Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces") (IDF) the "best" military force in the Middle East while at the same time suffering from "deficiencies" such as "immature doctrine, faulty logistics, and technical inadequacies".[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152) The IDF's Chief of Staff, Major General [Moshe Dayan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moshe_Dayan "Moshe Dayan"), encouraged aggression, initiative, and ingenuity among the Israeli officer corps while ignoring logistics and armoured operations.[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152) Dayan, a firm infantry man, preferred that arm of the service at the expense of armour, which Dayan saw as clumsy, pricey, and suffering from frequent breakdowns.[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152)

At the same time, the IDF had a rather disorganised logistics arm, which was put under severe strain when the IDF invaded the Sinai.[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152) Most of the IDF weapons in 1956 came from France.[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152) The main IDF tank was the AMX-13 and the main aircraft were the Dassault [Mystère IVA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dassault_Myst%C3%A8re_IV "Dassault Mystère IV") and the [Ouragan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dassault_Ouragan "Dassault Ouragan").[[148]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-153) Superior pilot training was to give the Israeli Air Force an unbeatable edge over their Egyptian opponents.[[147]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._18-152) The [Israeli Navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Navy "Israeli Navy") consisted of two destroyers, seven frigates, eight minesweepers, several landing craft, and fourteen torpedo boats.

### Egyptian

In the [Egyptian Armed Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Armed_Forces "Egyptian Armed Forces"), politics rather than military competence was the main criterion for promotion.[[149]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._19-154) The Egyptian commander, Field Marshal [Abdel Hakim Amer](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdel_Hakim_Amer "Abdel Hakim Amer"), was a purely political appointee who owed his position to his close friendship with Nasser. A heavy drinker, he would prove himself grossly incompetent as a general during the Crisis.[[149]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._19-154) In 1956, the Egyptian military was well equipped with weapons from the Soviet Union such as [T-34](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-34 "T-34") and [IS-3](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/IS_tank_family#IS-3 "IS tank family") tanks, [MiG-15](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/MiG-15 "MiG-15") fighters, [Ilyushin Il-28](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-28 "Ilyushin Il-28") bombers, [SU-100](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/SU-100 "SU-100") self-propelled guns and assault rifles.[[149]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._19-154)

Rigid lines between officers and men in the Egyptian Army led to a mutual "mistrust and contempt" between officers and the men who served under them.[[150]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._20-155) Egyptian troops were excellent in defensive operations, but had little capacity for offensive operations, owing to the lack of "rapport and effective small-unit leadership".[[150]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._20-155)

Invasion of Egypt
-----------------

Main article: [Timeline of the Suez Crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Suez_Crisis "Timeline of the Suez Crisis")

### Casualties

See also: [Khan Yunis massacre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khan_Yunis_massacre "Khan Yunis massacre")

British casualties stood at 22 dead[[151]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-:0-156)[[152]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-157) and 96 wounded,[[153]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Dupuy_1343-158) while French casualties were 10 dead and 33 wounded.[[151]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-:0-156)[[154]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-159) The Israeli losses were 172 dead and 817 wounded.[[2]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-LA_Times-2) The number of Egyptians killed was "never reliably established".[[155]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble,_Derek,_p._91-160) Egyptian casualties to the Israeli invasion were estimated at 1,000–3,000 dead and 4,000 wounded, while losses to the Anglo-French operation were estimated at 650 dead and 900 wounded.[[5]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchiff197470-5)[[156]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-161) 1,000 Egyptian civilians are estimated to have died.[[3]](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis#cite_note-Varble_1956,_p._90-3)

End of hostilities
------------------
